  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3bfb7840-bbe5-4b02-b335-d58cac844e97'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer507432702850821172"><b>A stunning, lyrical novel set in the rolling foothills of the Appalachians in which a young girl discovers stark truths that will haunt her for the rest of her life.</b><br/><br/> "A girl comes of age against the knife."<br/><br/> So begins the story of Betty Carpenter. Born in a bathtub in 1954 to a Cherokee father and white mother, Betty is the sixth of eight siblings. The world they inhabit is</span>
  <span id="freeText507432702850821172" style="display:none"><b>A stunning, lyrical novel set in the rolling foothills of the Appalachians in which a young girl discovers stark truths that will haunt her for the rest of her life.</b><br /><br /> "A girl comes of age against the knife."<br /><br /> So begins the story of Betty Carpenter. Born in a bathtub in 1954 to a Cherokee father and white mother, Betty is the sixth of eight siblings. The world they inhabit is one of poverty and violence--both from outside the family, and also, devastatingly, from within. The lush landscape, rich with birdsong, wild fruit, and blazing stars, becomes a kind of refuge for Betty, but when her family's darkest secrets are brought to light, she has no choice but to reckon with the brutal history hiding in the hills, as well as the heart-wrenching cruelties and incredible characters she encounters in her rural town of Breathed, Ohio.<br /><br /> But despite the hardship she faces, Betty is resilient. Her curiosity about the natural world, her fierce love for her sisters, and her father's brilliant stories are kindling for the fire of her own imagination, and in the face of all she bears witness to, Betty discovers an escape: she begins to write. She recounts the horrors of her family's past and present with pen and paper and buries them deep in the dirt--moments that has stung her so deeply, she could not tell them, until now.<br /><br /> Inspired by the life of her own mother, Tiffany McDaniel sets out to free the past by telling this heartbreaking yet magical story--a remarkable novel that establishes her as one of the freshest and most important voices in American fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="507432702850821172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

  <span id="freeText139044518827759182" style="display:none">NOW AVAILABLE!!! HEYYY YOU GUYS!!!! IT'S AVAILABLE!!!<br><br>i enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114523.The_Summer_that_Melted_Everything" title="The Summer that Melted Everything by Tiffany McDaniel" rel="nofollow noopener">The Summer that Melted Everything</a> a bunch, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/48564330.Betty" title="Betty by Tiffany McDaniel" rel="nofollow noopener">Betty</a>; a standalone with spillover into TSTME, has so much more weight. i remember bits and pieces from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114523.The_Summer_that_Melted_Everything" title="The Summer that Melted Everything by Tiffany McDaniel" rel="nofollow noopener">The Summer that Melted Everything</a>—i remember the language being striking, i remember the framework and a few details in particular, but this one is going to stay in my brain for a lot longer, and there are specific scenes i know are with me for life; not as fond memories of a book i enjoyed, but as straight-up reader scars. <br><br>for me, that’s a good thing, but some people’ll be too gentle for this book, and they will read it and low-star it because it made them too sad or uncomfortable but when you consider it's a family saga inspired by the life of mcdaniel’s own mother, it becomes like that joke about the man and the boy walking through the woods, where the boy says “hey mister, it’s getting dark and i’m scared.” and the man says “how do you think i feel, i have to walk back alone.” <br><br>[‘course, in this case, it would be a girl—there are so many ways a girl can hurt. and if <i>A girl comes of age against the knife</i> isn’t just begging to be tattooed across all the clavicles of lilith fair, i don’t know what is.] <br><br>in any event—i don’t know what is hand-on-bible truth here, or what has been inflated for dramatic effect, but even if everything in this book was conjured up out of the clear blue sky, day after day this world reminds us it is full of horrorshows and people who have survived things others are too lily-livered to even <i>read</i> about. and <i>that</i>, to me, seems insensitive. <br><br>this book is sad. it is SAD. it is beautiful and broken and filled with tenderness and love and cruelty and neglect and it is SEARING. i cannot emphasize enough that, like life, it is a mixture of sad and lovely. although, also like life, for every sad you see coming, there’ll be two that’ll catch you off guard. <br><br>i will admit, it took me a minute to get into it. the language isn’t as engorged as it was in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114523.The_Summer_that_Melted_Everything" title="The Summer that Melted Everything by Tiffany McDaniel" rel="nofollow noopener">The Summer that Melted Everything</a>, but there was something a little fiddly and twee to the beginning that didn’t grab me right away but once it did, i was thunderstruck, rapt, unable to look away &amp;etc. i belonged to it.<br><br>mcdaniel has excellent control of the narrative, handling foreshadowing and discovery like a boss, and making you care about (almost) every member of this family, even at their least sympathetic. <br><br>a loud recommend for this book. it did things to me. <br><br><blockquote>”God hates us.”<br><br>“The Carpenters?” I asked.<br><br>“Women.” She dabbed the lipstick against my lips, using her pinkie to smooth it into the corners. “He made us from the rib of man. That has been our curse ever since. Because of it, men have the shovel and we have the land. It’s right between our legs. There, they can bury all their sins. Bury ‘em so deep, no one knows about ‘em except for them and us.”<br><br>With a delicate step back she looked at me, her eyes cutting where they landed.<br><br>“My, my, Betty girl.” she smiled. “Red is not your color, darlin’.”</blockquote><br><br>*oh and p.s—whatever landon's “pudding pie” is; this wondrous magic of “multicolored gelatin cubes suspended in pink gelatin,” i want the recipe.*<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="139044518827759182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3449915457" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3449915457" />
    <a title="Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32340179-jennifer-tarheelreader"><img alt="Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463943779p2/32340179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3449915457?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader" href="/user/show/32340179-jennifer-tarheelreader">Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32340179-jennifer-tarheelreader?shelf=huggable-books">huggable-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32340179-jennifer-tarheelreader?shelf=recent-favorites">recent-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32340179-jennifer-tarheelreader?shelf=buddy-read-with-beth">buddy-read-with-beth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3449915457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13366823791056052946"><b>More than five-star worthy, my favorite book of summer 2020. </b> ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ <br/><br/>I read and loved The Summer That Melted Everything when it published four years ago. Incidentally, I won a copy of that book from a blog giveaway, and since it was autographed, I was put in contact with the author and quickly found she is as lovely and kind as I imagined she’d be. <br/><br/>When you read one of her books, now that I have two under my belt, I can say this with absolute certainty, the reader knows she has something</span>
  <span id="freeText13366823791056052946" style="display:none"><b>More than five-star worthy, my favorite book of summer 2020. </b> ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ <br /><br />I read and loved The Summer That Melted Everything when it published four years ago. Incidentally, I won a copy of that book from a blog giveaway, and since it was autographed, I was put in contact with the author and quickly found she is as lovely and kind as I imagined she’d be. <br /><br />When you read one of her books, now that I have two under my belt, I can say this with absolute certainty, the reader knows she has something special in her hands. Books don’t come written like this every day. Storytelling isn’t always this memorable. And you know all know I love books and authors, so at the heart of what I am saying is I absolutely adored this book. It’s THE book. My book of summer. <br /><br />Betty is a story based on the author’s mother’s life. It’s written in first person with Betty narrating. She shares the earliest history of both her parents, and then takes us through the family’s life as her siblings are born, before and after she is born, and up through the years as she comes-of-age. <br /><br />Growing up in the foothills of the Appalachian mountains, in small town, Breathed, Ohio, which is a character all its own, Betty’s first person narrative is an intimate storytelling. She brings us right into the story, alongside her dear family, and this family? They have a loving father named Landon, a Cherokee storyteller who passes his gift on to Betty (and likewise to Tiffany, the author). Every story he shares is a glorious explanation of the way the world works. This humble, dear, vulnerable, loving father? I don’t think I could love a character more. <br /><br />Betty’s mother, Alka, has a tormented past, and she has her share of difficulty with mental health as a result. The author writes about this with honesty and openness, while showing how most of the family adapts, supporting one another. There’s such tenderness between many of the characters, such complete devotion. There’s complexity, too, where their human nature comes into play, the push and pull so many families experience in their dynamic. No one is perfect, and Betty, with her insightful narrative doesn’t hide anything from the reader. Betty is bold and strong and completely authentic.<br /><br />The family experiences a number of difficulties, big heartbreaks, strife, and losses, and every single time, Betty gets back up again. And through all of that, the family has each other. Some of the siblings are present for each other the most loving way. Landon is there to comfort, guide, and believe in his children, when they struggle to find meaning themselves. <br /><br />When I was a mere 5% into this book, I fretted about not wanting it to end. This book is THAT good. The characters are living, breathing, loving, and endearing. They go through the darkest and most unsettling of times, and I was with them for every bit of this journey I never wanted to end.<br /><br />I voted for The Summer That Melted Everything to win every literary prize in 2016. I will be right there shouting from the rooftops that I loved this book. Please be aware that while I call this book beautiful in so many ways, dark things happen to and within this family. That is not what this book is about. Powerful, emotional, beautifully descriptive and haunting, I will never forget Betty, her indelible story, or the way she shared it through her daughter’s masterful skill.<br /><br />This review is a work in progress. I’ll be back to clean it up, and as I process more what this book means to me. ❤️ <br /><br />While I received a gifted copy early copy, I preordered both US and UK copies on my own. (Yes, I HAD to have the signed Waterstone’s special edition from the UK! Why doesn’t the US do more special editions?!) <br /><br />Many of my reviews can also be found on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jennifertarheelreader.com">www.jennifertarheelreader.com</a> and instagram: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.instagram.com/tarheelreader">www.instagram.com/tarheelreader</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13366823791056052946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3434077208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3434077208" />
    <a title="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews"><img alt="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472552597p2/54886546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3434077208?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" href="/user/show/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews">Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/49201494-betty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=traveling-sister-read">traveling-sister-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3434077208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer766716933942130151">4+ strong stars for this unforgettable story!<br/><br/>This is a story about family. Betty is the daughter of a white mother and Cherokee father. Of all her siblings, Betty develops the most physical traits of her Cherokee heritage. Betty’s father takes pride in teaching his children the stories of his ancestors and passing down his family traditions involving the healing powers of plants and herbs. Betty’s family struggles to fit in no matter where they live, but her family unit keeps her grounded and co</span>
  <span id="freeText766716933942130151" style="display:none">4+ strong stars for this unforgettable story!<br /><br />This is a story about family. Betty is the daughter of a white mother and Cherokee father. Of all her siblings, Betty develops the most physical traits of her Cherokee heritage. Betty’s father takes pride in teaching his children the stories of his ancestors and passing down his family traditions involving the healing powers of plants and herbs. Betty’s family struggles to fit in no matter where they live, but her family unit keeps her grounded and confident that things will get better. Based on the authors’ mothers’ life, this story is brutally honest, haunting and exceptionally well written.<br /><br />I will warn you that this is not a book to read if you are feeling emotionally vulnerable in any way. There are several ugly, gut wrenching, dark and horrific scenes. Yet, as uncomfortable as those scenes were to read, the exquisite writing pulled me so deeply inside this family that I simply couldn’t turn away from them. My heart ached for what this family endured, yet I remained hopeful for them. <br /><br />The main theme of the strong sense of family bond and loyalty was captured so perfectly. I was teary eyed more than a few times while experiencing the love and comfort these siblings offered each other.<br /><br />This was a sad but beautiful story that I highly recommend. Thank you to the author for sending me a review copy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="766716933942130151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3409607673" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3409607673" />
    <a title="Brenda - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10841164-brenda---traveling-sisters-book-reviews"><img alt="Brenda - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593373423p2/10841164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3409607673?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" href="/user/show/10841164-brenda---traveling-sisters-book-reviews">Brenda - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10841164-brenda---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=traveling-sister-reads">traveling-sister-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10841164-brenda---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=good-one-for-a-group-read">good-one-for-a-group-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3409607673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5232168960161361000">Tiffany McDaniel has joined us for a spoiler-free Q & A in our Behind the Pages and gave us some great insight into Betty's story and her journey to getting her story of the shelves. Don't miss reading what she has to say! <br/><br/>You can find the thread here<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/21666252-spoiler-free-q-a-tiffany-mcdaniel-author-of-betty'>https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br/><br/>Betty is a story inspired by Tiffany McDaniel's mother, Betty and her family secrets. It's a story of abuse, racism and poverty but a story of love through the strong connections Betty has with her father Land</span>
  <span id="freeText5232168960161361000" style="display:none">Tiffany McDaniel has joined us for a spoiler-free Q &amp; A in our Behind the Pages and gave us some great insight into Betty's story and her journey to getting her story of the shelves. Don't miss reading what she has to say! <br /><br />You can find the thread here<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/21666252-spoiler-free-q-a-tiffany-mcdaniel-author-of-betty">https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br /><br />Betty is a story inspired by Tiffany McDaniel's mother, Betty and her family secrets. It's a story of abuse, racism and poverty but a story of love through the strong connections Betty has with her father Landon and her siblings. It's also an Appalachian story with Cherokee stories and history. It's not an easy read at times and might not be for the lighter more gentle minded reader; however, it's one of those stories that shows us the dark to see the light in the world around us.<br /><br />It is remarkable, stunningly and shockingly sad and heartbreaking, filled with as much love as it is devasting. It's the beautiful way it's written that made it impressive to me. We see the horrors of Betty's family past and present and my emotions ran wild with the cruelty inflicted on the characters. With Tiffany's use of words, I could see the beauty she and Betty found in love, family, Betty's father's stories and their connection to the Appalachian land. I could feel Tiffany's passion for telling Betty's family's story with all its beauty and ugliness. <br /><br />"I remember the fierce love and devotion as much as I remember the violence." "our family tree grew with rotten, broken branches and fungus on the leaves."<br /><br />Tiffany McDaniel takes her time here as she paints us a vivid picture of the stories Landan shares with Betty and his ways. The story is rich in the everyday life of the characters that is as bold as it is normal. At times it did feel a bit much for me, making the book feel longer than it needed to be and at times, I lost some focus. <br /><br />At times the sadness might feel relentless because it's so horrifying but I thought Tiffany McDaniel balanced it with the love, connections and stories she shared with us through Landon. I kept imagining how relentless the violence might have felt for Tiffany and Betty and how much courage they both had in telling their stories. <br /><br />This is a story that is as beautiful as it is ugly! <br /><br />I received a copy from Tiffany McDaniel to read and review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5232168960161361000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3559186089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3559186089" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3559186089?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=2020-release">2020-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=gifted">gifted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=all-the-stars-in-the-sky">all-the-stars-in-the-sky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=cross-post">cross-post</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=faves-adult-historical-fiction">faves-adult-historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3559186089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11459322295026884095"><blockquote>“When I was your age, I wanted to be someone else too.”<br/>“Who’d you wanna be, Dad?”<br/>“Someone important. You know why I call you Little Indian? So that you know you’re already someone important.”</blockquote><br/><br/>This is the story of Betty Carpenter and her family as they move from place to place until they finally settle in Breathed, Ohio on the foothills of the Appalachian mountains.<br/><br/>The Carpenters don’t fit in anywhere. Betty’s father, Landon, is Cherokee and her mother, Alka, is white. Betty, of all of her sibling</span>
  <span id="freeText11459322295026884095" style="display:none"><blockquote>“When I was your age, I wanted to be someone else too.”<br />“Who’d you wanna be, Dad?”<br />“Someone important. You know why I call you Little Indian? So that you know you’re already someone important.”</blockquote><br /><br />This is the story of Betty Carpenter and her family as they move from place to place until they finally settle in Breathed, Ohio on the foothills of the Appalachian mountains.<br /><br />The Carpenters don’t fit in anywhere. Betty’s father, Landon, is Cherokee and her mother, Alka, is white. Betty, of all of her siblings inherited the most of her fathers Cherokee features finds it hard to blend in and come to terms with her place in the world. She finds solace and comfort in her family and Landon’s stories as he teaches his children to love the land and to never forget their ancestors and where they came from.<br /><br />Through the years of poverty and struggle in Breathed, Betty witnesses horrors of cruelty and violence. Needing an escape she writes these events down, tells the stories of her family’s dark past and present, and buries it deep in the ground.<br /><br />We follow the family from the 1930s — the moment Landon and Alka meet — until Betty, their youngest daughter enters adulthood.<br /><br /><br /><br />This book was equally hard to read and magical at the same time. The first thing that swept me away was the writing. <b>It was enchanting and lyricle. Poetic and mesmerising.</b><br /><br />I don’t know if it’s because this book was more personal to the author or what? — but the way she wrote the setting and the characters was spectacular. It all felt so real and <b>the characters each felt so distinct.</b><br /><br />Some characters I hated with all my guts (if you know, you know 👀). And others I loved with all my heart: first and foremost being Landon, Betty’s dad.<br /><br />It was such a pleasure reading about him. Everything he taught his kids, his stories. I just- *sniffles* – love him so much.<br /><br /><blockquote>‘I realized then that not only did Dad need us to believe his stories, we needed to believe them as well. To believe in unripe stars and eagles able to do extraordinary things. What it boiled down to was a frenzied hope that there was more to life than the reality around us. Only then could we claim a destiny we did not feel cursed to.’</blockquote><br /><br />Betty herself was also such an amazing character. Her resilience in the face all she witnessed at such a young age had me astounded. This small girl, had to bear the burden of others and still she was so pure and brave.<br /><br />As I said there were difficult scenes in this book. Personally I dislike stumbling onto a scene and having it take me off guard. I’d prefer to know what I’m getting into. So I feel I should warn you if you’re going to pick this up that there are scenes of incestuous rape. I’ll leave the content warnings below 👇.<br /><br /><i>Betty</i> was filled with hard truths and brutal honesty. But don’t let that discourage you from picking this up. I am glad I went into Betty with my eyes open. It would have upset me more if I had not expected the more graphic scenes, but I knew to look out for them.<br /><br />This book is in fact based on the true story of the authors mother, Betty. Reading her dedication and her acknowledgements at the end of the book touched my heart.<br /><br />I am going to try to get my hands on the authors debut novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114523.The_Summer_that_Melted_Everything" title="The Summer that Melted Everything by Tiffany McDaniel" rel="nofollow noopener">The Summer that Melted Everything</a>, which was also set in the same town. I am officially obsessed with Tiffany McDaniel’s writing!! <br /><br /><i>Betty</i> is one of the best books I’ve read this year and will be added to my favourites list! And I will talk about it non stop to the point where everyone will be annoyed with me so they’ll read the book just to get me to be quiet ✌<br /><br /><b>CONTENT WARNINGS: violence; child abuse; animal abuse; incest; rape; suicide; abortion</b><br /><br /><i>« Thank you to the publishers for sending me this copy for review »</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11459322295026884095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3341357499" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3341357499" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3341357499?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3341357499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer234100991170928700">BETTY, by Tiffany McDaniel, will be a book that will bring forth reviews loaded with what will seem like hyperbole. Then you'll read it for yourself and understand that no one is exagerrating when they say that this book destroyed them, that it is a beautiful yet horrific masterpiece, that you have never read anything quite like it. <br/><br/>The first note I'd like to make is: that unassuming cover is going to lure in a lot of unsuspecting readers. BETTY is a horror novel. There's dread and terror on alm</span>
  <span id="freeText234100991170928700" style="display:none">BETTY, by Tiffany McDaniel, will be a book that will bring forth reviews loaded with what will seem like hyperbole. Then you'll read it for yourself and understand that no one is exagerrating when they say that this book destroyed them, that it is a beautiful yet horrific masterpiece, that you have never read anything quite like it. <br /><br />The first note I'd like to make is: that unassuming cover is going to lure in a lot of unsuspecting readers. BETTY is a horror novel. There's dread and terror on almost every page, and that's because the characters are so wonderfully crafted. Numerous times while reading, I had to set my phone down (I only WISH I'd gotten a physical ARC of this beauty, and you better believe I have the hardcover pre-ordered) and find something funny to watch on YouTube, or pick up one of the lighter books I was reading, which is odd for me, because I love darkness. You could even say it's an old friend of mine. But one person can only take so much. If you have any triggers whatsoever, here's your content warning: THEY ARE ALL IN THIS BOOK.<br /><br />BETTY is such an affecting piece of literature that I almost want to dislike it. This was not a pleasant read. I'd say that 70% of the novel is tragedy and sorrow, and some of the most disturbing body horror outside of, well, the horror genre. I don't mean to scare off readers of general fiction, or detract from McDaniel's literary capabilities, because they are tremendous, she's one of the best writers working today, but I can't place this elsewhere. Is it genre horror? No. Is it splatterpunk, or a creature feature? No. This is horror with a depth of heart, and that's what makes it so scary. You know bad things are going to happen to these people, most of who are lovely human beings, and it fills you with an unbearable amount of dread. Then, when the horror does strike, it's somehow even worse than you could imagine. Time and time again, I said to myself, "Self, no way things get any worse for this family. No way. Nu uh." And then it would. This book is exhausting in the best possible way.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, though, that other 30% is gorgeous, but so is the horrific content. This juxtaposition comes from McDaniel's ability to make the most mundane task magical with a set of perfectly chosen words, her ability to wax lyrical until the entirety of the novel shines. Every line is artwork, each paragraph a blessing, and every page a revelation. <br /><br />Landon Carpenter stole the show for me, though, if I'm completely honest. This is a novel of female burden and female pain, but the centerpiece of this well-organized table is Betty's father, a Cherokee man that reminded me very much of a kinder, gentler version of my father. My own dad was half Cherokee, because his father, the chief of his tribe, went out and married a redhead. Unlike Landon Carpenter, my father was an emotionally broken man and a complete terror to live with. While, like Landon, my father always had a story to tell, his attitude leaned more to a vicious nature. In that way, he was more like Betty's mother. <br /><br />The final parallel to my own life is how a certain character dies. This character's fate mirrored what my mother went through in February of this year (2020) so accurately, I had to put the book down for a few days. It hurt to read, and it hurts to think about now. <br /><br />In summation: This novel is a journey through beauty and magic, tragedy and horror, and damn near covers every trial and tribulation a family can go through. But where I think the book truly shines is that it begs you to find the light in the world, especially when that light is reduced to a single star in an otherwise pitch-black sky. BETTY shows you the worst so that you can appreciate the best, and I love it for that. My highest possible recommendation.<br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: Not only is this the best book I have read this year, but it's one of the best books I've read in my lifetime. </b><br /><br /><i>Many thanks to my buddy Aaron Nash for reading this one with me, and to the author for providing me with a copy for review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="234100991170928700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3386458706" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3386458706" />
    <a title="Cheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106692-cheri"><img alt="Cheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601402708p2/106692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3386458706?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheri" href="/user/show/106692-cheri">Cheri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/49201494-betty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=arkansas">arkansas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=native-american">native-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=ohio">ohio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=southern-lit">southern-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=racism">racism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=rape">rape</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=1960s">1960s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3386458706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14032699264650324990"><i>’I’m a child, only as tall as my father’s shotgun…When I sit next to him, I can feel the summer heat coming off his skin like he’s just another tin roof on a hot day.’</i><br/><br/>Her mother tells her stories, dark, filled with ominous warnings about what life is like for women. She knows from experience. Her father tells her stories, too, some from his family, Cherokee legends, and some from his heart - and one <i>about</i> his heart - a heart that is made of glass. When she asks how a piece of glass is inside him</span>
  <span id="freeText14032699264650324990" style="display:none"><i>’I’m a child, only as tall as my father’s shotgun…When I sit next to him, I can feel the summer heat coming off his skin like he’s just another tin roof on a hot day.’</i><br /><br />Her mother tells her stories, dark, filled with ominous warnings about what life is like for women. She knows from experience. Her father tells her stories, too, some from his family, Cherokee legends, and some from his heart - and one <i>about</i> his heart - a heart that is made of glass. When she asks how a piece of glass is inside him, he tells her:<br /><br /><i>’It’s hanging’ in there from a sweet little string. Within the glass is the bird God caught all the way up in heaven.’<br />‘Why’d He put a bird in there?’</i> she asks.<br /><i>So a little piece of heaven would always be in our hearts. Safest place for a piece of heaven, I reckon.</i><br /><br />And when he lays her head on his chest, asking her if she knows what that sound is from, she tells him it’s the beating of his heart, but he replies that <i>’It’s the noise of the little bird flappin’ her wings.’</i><br /><br />But this story is Betty’s, and it’s quite a story she has to tell. A story filled with her love for her father and her sisters, especially, but also with racism, and the many scars of childhood, and life. Coming from a family of eight children, Betty has five older siblings, when she is born, in a bathtub, in Ozark, Arkansas in 1954. Two younger siblings will follow, and money is tight, and that’s when this story really begins to take shape, after the youngest, Lint, was born and they decide to move, again. They are living in an old, rundown house that they bought sight unseen, in the southern Appalachia town of Breathed, Ohio, the location of the author’s debut novel <i>The Summer That Melted Everything.</i> settling in Breathed. Tales of older times pop up now and then, some of which serve as a warning. <br /><br />There’s so much love in this story, as well as things to love. I loved the stage that Betty’s father builds for her and her sisters, one like his mother had in her garden, and the garden of her mother, and so on <i>back to the beginnin’ of time</i> where the women and girls would sing to keep the crows and insects away. Their singing <i>seeped into the ground,</i> enriching the soil, and the garden thrived from their songs. Men and boys weren’t included, since it was the girls and women chosen, the ones given the power that Nature recognized. <br /><br />For every time this story broke my heart, McDaniel pieced it back together again. I loved the connection that Betty has with her sisters despite how broken they seem to be at times, how desperate they are to escape this place and be seen as being worthy of love, but especially with her father. I loved that despite everything in her life that might break another person, Betty seems to bear the burdens, and to thrive despite the adversity. The stories of her father offering her solace and fuels her desire to be more like him, to be a storyteller.<br /><br /><br /><br />Pub Date: 18 Aug 2020<br /><br />Many thanks for the ARC provided by Knopf / Random House</span>
  <a data-text-id="14032699264650324990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3386458706">

  <span id="freeText6209099603151230128" style="display:none">Incredible book!!!<br />Brutal....<br />Beautiful ...<br />Betty ... BETTY... Betty....<br /> ....I’ll never forget Betty and this gorgeously written story. <br /><br />This coming-of-age story about a girl of mixed race ...based on the authors real life family history...(her mother, *Betty*, at the heart of Tiffany McDaniel’s inspiration), is masterfully told. <br /><br />It deals with abuse, sexual abuse, racism, poverty, prejudice, family secrets, guilt, sexism, suicide, and other family tragedies. <br />Historically epic... this family saga is emotional....<br />It’s beauty and love shines through the exceptional storytelling...<br />Fantastic characters and dialogue...<br />...Nature to dig your teeth into...<br /> ...rather ‘hands-and-feet’ in the rich soil of the earth...<br />...Magical and moving Cherokee myths &amp; legends: deeply touching tales a father, (Landon), passes on to Betty...<br />... memorable scenes I’ll never forget: mama making homemade noodles in her kitchen while barefoot....<br />...Betty and her siblings..<br /> be it in the woods or in their house: ( sometimes the story had a childlike fairytale ‘feel’)... but with the devastations - it’s not a child’s book) <br /><br />I was left breathless...<br />...It’s enchanting and devastating...<br />...beautiful and cruel<br />... intensified sadness with vicious acts...<br />But....<br />the strength and dreams for a better life...in the rolling hills of the Ohio Appalachians is like a rising sun of brightness. <br /><br />“A girl comes of age against the knife. She must learn to bear its blade. To be cut. To bleed. To scar over and still,<br />somehow be beautiful and with good enough knees to take the sponge of the kitchen floor every Saturday...<br />I remember the fierce love and devotion as much as I remember the violence”. <br /><br />5+++++ stars<br />A years favorite!!!!!</span>

<div id="review_3514023485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3514023485" />
    <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic"><img alt="Irena BookDustMagic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362943196p2/17737927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3514023485?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irena BookDustMagic" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic">Irena BookDustMagic</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3514023485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7010651996164971450">Trigger warning: this book talks about racism, have graphic scenes about bullying and violence, talks about child loss, abuse, suicide, and also has homophobic lines that are part of the story.<br/><br/>Back in 2016 I read McDaniel's debut novel The Summer That Melted Everything and it is now one of my all time favourite reads. I knew then that I want to read everything she publishes in the future.<br/><br/>This year we were lucky to see her second novel published, Betty, that was in reality the first novel she wro</span>
  <span id="freeText7010651996164971450" style="display:none">Trigger warning: this book talks about racism, have graphic scenes about bullying and violence, talks about child loss, abuse, suicide, and also has homophobic lines that are part of the story.<br /><br />Back in 2016 I read McDaniel's debut novel The Summer That Melted Everything and it is now one of my all time favourite reads. I knew then that I want to read everything she publishes in the future.<br /><br />This year we were lucky to see her second novel published, Betty, that was in reality the first novel she wrote several years ago.<br /><br />Betty is based on the life of Tiffany McDaniel's mother, and even though it is fiction, many scenes and most of the story are based on the real life.<br /><br />Therefore I decided I won't give this book a rating.<br />I have a rule that I don't rate non fiction, and because this novel is based on someone else's life, I don't feel comfortable to judge the story.<br /><br />However, I will tell you my feelings and experience with it.<br /><br />Betty was extremely emotional and heartbreaking story. <br />I saw people compare it to A Little Life, the book I still haven't read, but it is well known for the sadness, so it makes sense.<br /><br />I think it is important to say that this is own voices in a way. It talks about the girl who is Cherokee (her father was Cherokee and mother was white). <br />I know it's not the author's job to teach us but we should all inform ourselves, but I still want to mention that I learned from this book more then I have before from movies (we don't learn American history in Croatian schools).<br /><br />I still can't believe how racist people were and how awful they treated people just because they had different skin color and came with a different culture.<br />I still can't believe the cruelty Betty had to go through, and my heart was breaking for her.<br /><br />There are also some parts in the book that were extremely difficult to read.<br />I had to stop at some parts and even skipped some because they were triggering for me (suicidal thoughts plus difficult relationship with mother).<br /><br />This book is very important, but not everyone can handle it, in my opinion.<br /><br />I read in an article that it took 10+ years for the book to get published, and I believe now it is good time for the Betty to come out, when more people want to read about different cultures and diversity, and when own voices are finally heard.<br />I also think that Betty should have been promoted more, because it deserves more attention, but I hope as people'll read it they will talk about it more and it will get the recognition.<br /><br />The last thing I want to praise is McDaniel's voice. Her style is lyrical and beautiful, but also very forward.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to lovers of literary fiction, but also to readers who'd like to read diverse books.<br />But guard yourself with some tissues because you'll need them!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7010651996164971450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3393256545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3393256545" />
    <a title="Betsy Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5149179-betsy-robinson"><img alt="Betsy Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404493492p2/5149179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3393256545?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betsy Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betsy Robinson" href="/user/show/5149179-betsy-robinson">Betsy Robinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/49201494-betty">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3393256545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8410973749014124808">There is a level of emotional pain that I find almost unbearable—usually evoked by stories of animal or child abuse. The only remedy for me, other than shutting down completely, is vacuuming. Suffice it to say that the experience reading <i>Betty</i> left me with the cleanest carpet and wood floor I've ever had.<br/><br/>The book was at times so excruciating that I had to stop reading and not only clean but lie on the couch and pant in pain. Nevertheless, this is a very good novel—a story based on the author's m</span>
  <span id="freeText8410973749014124808" style="display:none">There is a level of emotional pain that I find almost unbearable—usually evoked by stories of animal or child abuse. The only remedy for me, other than shutting down completely, is vacuuming. Suffice it to say that the experience reading <i>Betty</i> left me with the cleanest carpet and wood floor I've ever had.<br /><br />The book was at times so excruciating that I had to stop reading and not only clean but lie on the couch and pant in pain. Nevertheless, this is a very good novel—a story based on the author's mother's childhood. A story of the abuse white culture heaps on Native people. That men heap on women and children. That crazy people heap on every living thing. It is well written, very different from Tiffany McDaniel's first published novel, <i>The Summer that Melted Everything</i>, but birthed way earlier (and its ending makes it seem like a prequel to the first novel). <i>Betty</i> starts out as a child's story, and had it stayed that way, I might have lost interest. But the writer's mature skill moved it into the adult fiction category, with one of the lovingest father characters I've ever read.<br /><br />*ARC provided by publisher.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8410973749014124808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3346191491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3346191491" />
    <a title="Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70046142-elle"><img alt="Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548160841p2/70046142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3346191491?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle" href="/user/show/70046142-elle">Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70046142-elle?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70046142-elle?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3346191491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5514131078271296073">I’m left utterly breathless. What an immense story contained within a singular family. I don’t know if there’s a way to adequately prepare someone to go into this novel, but here I’ll do my best.<br/><br/>“<i>You know what the heaviest thing in the world is, Betty?</i>”<br/><br/>This book was the quiet before the storm, and then it was the storm itself. Tiffany McDaniel‘s writing is exquisite. There’s a way that authors-who-are-also-poets write that’s almost immediately identifiable. It felt like every other line containe</span>
  <span id="freeText5514131078271296073" style="display:none">I’m left utterly breathless. What an immense story contained within a singular family. I don’t know if there’s a way to adequately prepare someone to go into this novel, but here I’ll do my best.<br /><br />“<i>You know what the heaviest thing in the world is, Betty?</i>”<br /><br />This book was the quiet before the storm, and then it was the storm itself. Tiffany McDaniel‘s writing is exquisite. There’s a way that authors-who-are-also-poets write that’s almost immediately identifiable. It felt like every other line contained something that I want to scribble down and store away for later. But as soon as I found myself falling into a rhythm, the song quickly shifted into a new movement, and I was thrown off the beat. As easily as she can sweep you away, McDaniel can yank you suddenly back into your body.<br /><br /><i>Betty</i> follows the life of Betty Carpenter and her family as she grows up in the fictional town of Breathed, Ohio. Her father, Landon, is Cherokee and her mother, Alka is white. Every significant moment in their lives from the time the two of them meet until the final pages of the book is documented by their youngest daughter, Betty, as she learns about who she is and what her place is in the world. Most of these lessons are hard, made harder by the time and location she resides in. But they are also made easier by the fortifying nature of some of her family members and ancestors. <br /><br />This is not a story of family drama but one of family trauma. It’s also the story of all the beautiful things that grow in the cracks between them. In the Carpenters, we watch as the scars of one generation are passed on to the next. It can be hard to reconcile when a person unloads that pain onto someone they’re supposed to love unconditionally. Can you forgive someone that’s tried to drag you down with them, if they thought it was the only way they could keep from drowning? Can any amount of understanding make it okay? It will never be okay. <br /><br />Parts of this book were devastating. Other parts were enchanting. I don’t want to giveaway any plot, but I also don’t want someone to go in entirely blind. Give yourself the emotional space to fully immerse yourself in the story. There is grief and there is joy. There are storms and there is solace. There are beginnings and there are endings. We can’t choose what we inherit or from who, but we do have some say in what we do with it. <br /><br /><br /><i>I wasn’t sure whether or not to include trigger warnings, as some may be considered spoilers, but I also didn’t want to make that choice for someone. Here I’ve hidden them in a spoiler tag, so the decision is up to you: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ abortion, animal abuse, child abuse, death, homophobia, incest, racism, sexual violence, suicide <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></i><br /><br /><br /><i>*Thanks to Tiffany McDaniel, Knopf Doubleday Publishing &amp; Netgalley for advance review copies!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5514131078271296073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3473966268" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3473966268" />
    <a title="MicheleReader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28862120-michelereader"><img alt="MicheleReader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549899164p2/28862120.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3473966268?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MicheleReader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MicheleReader" href="/user/show/28862120-michelereader">MicheleReader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/49201494-betty">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3473966268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15112991854647090692">Tiffany McDaniel’s incredible novel <b>Betty</b> broke me. It’s the coming-of-age story of Betty Carpenter. Born in a bathtub in 1954, Betty, the sixth of eight children, was raised for most of her life in the foothills of the Ohio Appalachians. Her father Landon Carpenter is a proud Cherokee married to her mother, Alka Lark, who is white. While her siblings look more like her mother, Betty is most like her father with dark skin. <br/><br/>The family is poor but Landon provides his children with inventive storyt</span>
  <span id="freeText15112991854647090692" style="display:none">Tiffany McDaniel’s incredible novel <b>Betty</b> broke me. It’s the coming-of-age story of Betty Carpenter. Born in a bathtub in 1954, Betty, the sixth of eight children, was raised for most of her life in the foothills of the Ohio Appalachians. Her father Landon Carpenter is a proud Cherokee married to her mother, Alka Lark, who is white. While her siblings look more like her mother, Betty is most like her father with dark skin. <br /><br />The family is poor but Landon provides his children with inventive storytelling rooted in Cherokee myths and legends. From blazing stars to a bird living in a glass heart, the stories are magical. Betty develops a creative mind and becomes a storyteller in her own right. The support and love, especially from her father, does not prepare Betty for the hatred she faces once she enters school. Betty experiences racial hatred not only from the other children but from the faculty. While her mother tells Betty that she is not pretty like her sisters, it is the sweet and wonderful relationship with her father that keeps Betty strong and believing in herself. <br /><br />Betty comes to learn the truth of generational abuse hidden within her own family shaking her entire foundation. It is way too much for a child to deal with this type of trauma and it’s very hard to read about it.<br /><br /><b>Betty</b> is based on the author’s mother Betty and her family which makes the story even more heartbreaking. The writing is stunning and lyrical. I kept noting favorite passages when I realized almost every word in this book is worth savoring. It is rare for a book to stir up so much emotion. I highly recommend this book.<br /><br />I am so glad that the author reached out to me to read <b>Betty</b> in advance of its publication. Thank you, thank you Tiffany McDaniel. And thanks to Knopf Doubleday Publishing Group / Random House and NetGalley.<br /><br /><i>Content Warning: the book includes some passages of sexual abuse that might be too disturbing for some readers.</i><br /><br />Review posted on <a href="https://www.michelereader.com/post/betty-an-unforgettable-story-that-is-both-tragic-and-hopeful" rel="nofollow noopener">MicheleReader.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15112991854647090692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6793065083731705251">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>

</b><br/><br/>Between the ‘Rona being errrrywhere and homeschooling (both high school and college versions) and entirely new systems at work despite no one <i>being</i> at actual work, I haven’t been on here in a hot minute. Buuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuut I’m still reading like a maniac and <b>had</b> to say a lil’ summi</span>
  <span id="freeText6793065083731705251" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i>"Don't you wish you had a sack full of good days, Betty? Whenever you were havin' a bad day you could reach into the sack and make everything better."</i>
</b><br><br>Between the ‘Rona being errrrywhere and homeschooling (both high school and college versions) and entirely new systems at work despite no one <i>being</i> at actual work, I haven’t been on here in a hot minute. Buuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuut I’m still reading like a maniac and <b>had</b> to say a lil’ summin about <i>Betty</i>. Pause for a brief synopsis . . . . .<br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599755700ra/30088712.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Srsly. Oh poor Betty. My notes are full of “holy shits” and “make me stop feeling things, you fucker” (that last one was specifically for Tiffany McDaniel). In case you aren’t familiar with this novel, it’s a fictional biography inspired by the life of the author’s mother that spans from 1901 to 1973. It’s about family and race and class and prejudice and evils of men (and women) and life in Appalachia and a little folklore and a spot of ‘shine. And it is a nearly 500 page kick in the face. But somewhere in all that misery is a little hope and humor as well. Hope in the form of the best daddy I've ever met and humor in Betty herself . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>"I've never seen a colored before."<br><br>"And I've never seen a butt for a face before but if you don't turn around right now, I'm gonna take my daddy's pocketknife and cut you up into tiny pieces to mail to your momma in a heart-shaped box."</i>
</b><br> <br>I’ve had <i>The Summer That Everything Melted</i> on my Kindle as an advanced copy since well before its release date, but continue to avoid it like the black plague due to fear of disappointing either <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1595075533?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Bestie</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1703909706?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Nemesis</a> when I read it wrong. I’m not going to make any promises that I’ll bump it up the TBR anytime soon, but after reading <i>Betty</i> I think I would likely lean more toward Shelby’s side of the fence.<br><br>This book is not going to be for everyone. In case you aren’t familiar with me, I don’t shy away from dark subject matter and when I say this one is brutal, I’m not kidding. Absolutely no punches were pulled so if you are of the sensitive nature or require your reviews come with a trigger warning, consider this your notice that EVERY trigger will be triggered.<br><br>4.5 Stars rather than 5 because it was just a <i>weeeeee</i> bit long in the tooth and not every page was necessary.</span>

<div id="review_3357336810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3357336810" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3357336810?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3357336810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16265255385234892544">“Boys are like that. Always tryin’ to pretend they’re savin’ girls from somethin’. They never seem to realize, we can save ourselves.”<br/><br/>First of all, HUGE thank you to @orionbooks for this review copy! Chalk it up now: Tiffany McDaniel is a REAL bonafide talent. The Summer That Melted Everything was not a one-off masterpiece - McDaniel is here to stay.<br/><br/>Betty is a coming-of-age tale based upon McDaniel’s mother’s upbringing in the foothills of the Appalachian Mountains. Heavily infused with the stun</span>
  <span id="freeText16265255385234892544" style="display:none">“Boys are like that. Always tryin’ to pretend they’re savin’ girls from somethin’. They never seem to realize, we can save ourselves.”<br /><br />First of all, HUGE thank you to @orionbooks for this review copy! Chalk it up now: Tiffany McDaniel is a REAL bonafide talent. The Summer That Melted Everything was not a one-off masterpiece - McDaniel is here to stay.<br /><br />Betty is a coming-of-age tale based upon McDaniel’s mother’s upbringing in the foothills of the Appalachian Mountains. Heavily infused with the stunning storytelling and culture of the Cherokee people, Betty is the story of the Carpenter family.<br /><br />In a nutshell, if you loved TSTME, there’s a great chance you’ll fall head over heels for this story too. Once again Tiffany manages to explore a multitude of heavy themes including rape, incest, sexual abuse, racism, poverty and so forth, through her beautifully poetic prose. But as you can see, there are many trigger warnings for this one!<br /><br />One of my favourite things about McDaniel’s work so far is the depiction of the magical father-son/daughter relationships she writes into her stories. Personally this is a sensitive spot for me, having lost my father at a relatively young age, so I take extra pleasure in reading about and imagining what such a relationship could look like. This book is sad. It’s heartbreaking and tragic, it will break your heart in two, but Betty’s relationship with her father is one of the lights that shines through all the darkness. As is her relationship with her sisters (most of the time!).<br /><br />Admittedly it took me a while to get into Betty at the beginning. I struggled a little when it came to grasping the Cherokee culture and history as I’m simply not familiar with it, but once I did, those stories were very moving.<br /><br />McDaniel is quickly becoming an all-time favourite author - I’d recommend this one wholeheartedly! (But be mindful of the trigger warnings, of course) 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16265255385234892544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=dark-fiction">dark-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=ladiesofhorrorfiction">ladiesofhorrorfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror-adjacent">horror-adjacent</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3410570934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4396517542268473191">*I received an ARC from Netgalley with the unspoken promise I'd write a review. Here it is.<br/><br/>I said this about The Summer That Melted Everything and I’m going to say the exact same thing about Betty. “This story is cruel, it is bleak and it is beautifully descriptive and impossible to put down.” If you haven’t read the work of Tiffany McDaniel you are truly missing out because her prose is pure magic and I am not exaggerating. These two books deserve every single star in the reviewing universe.<br/><br/>Bet</span>
  <span id="freeText4396517542268473191" style="display:none">*I received an ARC from Netgalley with the unspoken promise I'd write a review. Here it is.<br /><br />I said this about The Summer That Melted Everything and I’m going to say the exact same thing about Betty. “This story is cruel, it is bleak and it is beautifully descriptive and impossible to put down.” If you haven’t read the work of Tiffany McDaniel you are truly missing out because her prose is pure magic and I am not exaggerating. These two books deserve every single star in the reviewing universe.<br /><br />Betty is inspired by McDaniel’s own mother and it is a powerhouse of a novel. It is set in the same town of Blessed as The Summer That Melted Everything so if you’ve read that book (and trust me you need to read that book), you’ll recognize the setting and there are several nods to TSTME near the end.<br /><br />This is the coming of age story of Betty, a sensitive and wise young soul, who was born in a bathtub in 1954 to a white mother and a full-blooded Cherokee father and surrounded by older and younger siblings. Betty shares the dark skin, eyes, and hair color as her beloved father, and as she grows she faces prejudice and hateful bullying but her father’s love, kindness and stories inspire her to overcome and she never allows the suffocating hatred and unfairness of her circumstances to destroy her - even when she has all the reason in the world to do so. She is smart and strong and has a barbed wit that serves her well in life. Life is difficult for Betty. The things she endures would ruin most of us.<br /><br />This book skillfully blends beauty and cruelty and doles them both out in equal measure. I’m not going to sugar coat things because that’s not what I do. Within these pages are some of the most devastating scenes I’ve ever read and I’ve read many a grueling book because I am a glutton for that kind of soul-shredding pain. There is one particular scene here that will be burned into my memory until my final days. Betty is hard to read and it is emotionally gutting and if you have any triggers please be warned that this book likely contains all of them. I had to put it down multiple times to take a breather and read something a little lighter but I never regretted going back to it. Life is ugly and life is cruel but life is also filled with joy and laughter and love and hope.<br /><br />Betty is a story of abuse and it’s long-lasting repercussions, of trauma and poverty, prejudice, and crushing grief but even more so it’s a love letter to a wonderful man and a strong young woman. It’s bleak and devastating and far more horrible than most any horror novel I’ve ever read (and I’ve likely read far too many!) but it’s also filled with beautiful traditions, an incredible amount of wisdom, love, beauty, resilience, and hope. You’re going to feel broken and beaten as you read the words McDaniel has put down on these pages but Betty is one of those books you will not be able to stop thinking about and one you will not regret reading after you’ve turned the final page.<br /><br />There are so many gorgeous and quotable passages here but this one struck me the hardest and made my heart stop a minute with its raw, powerful, and blunt imagery.<br /><br />“She’s going to scream, I thought. And it’ll be something real. Something we have to chain up in the backyard and feed with bloody steaks.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="4396517542268473191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11727270010084303583">The haunting story of young Betty Carpenter growing up in a small town in Ohio, in the foothills of the Appalachian range.   <span id="freeText11727270010084303583" style="display:none">The haunting story of young Betty Carpenter growing up in a small town in Ohio, in the foothills of the Appalachian range. Born in 1954, Betty is the sixth of eight children born to Landon Carpenter, a proud Cherokee father, who rescues their white mother, Alka Lark, from a bad home. Sadly for Betty, she looks like her father and is the subject of discrimination because of her dark skin, whereas her siblings look like her mother. Each of her siblings has his/her own issues, which is to a large extent, managed skillfully by their father’s love and his children inventive storytelling based in Cherokee myths and legends and his wonderful imagination. Alka, the mother is so fundamentally damaged that she is unable to provide supplemental love. Nonetheless, Betty develops a creative mind and becomes a talented storyteller in her own right.<br /><br />Strife, abuse, poverty, guilt, and tragedy are recurring themes of this very well written saga, which for me anyway, was reminiscent of one of my most favorite books of all time: Pat Conroy’s <i>The Prince of Tides.</i> This book is deserved of receiving notoriety and awards, which I hope it receives. 4.5 stars rounded up.</span>
